Control Yuan Impeaches Two Public Officials 44

Wu Zhilian and Yu Shunqian Neglect Their Duties and Betray the Country

The Control Yuan's impeachment case against Wu Zhilian, Secretary of the Judicial Yuan, and Yu Shunqian, Director of the Jing City Land Bureau, for neglecting their duties and betraying the country, is presented as follows: "According to a proposal by Control Yuan member Wang Pingzheng, an investigation was conducted based on a complaint from citizen Ye Fuying and others accusing Wu Zhilian, Secretary of the Judicial Yuan, and Yu Shunqian, Director of the Nanjing Municipal Government Land Bureau, of neglecting their duties and betraying the country. This Yuan dispatched Secretary Zhang Gongzhen to investigate. According to the report, it was found that Wu Zhilian, in the name of the agent of the Japanese Saito Risuke, applied to the Jing City Land Bureau in August of this year to survey multiple acres of land in the area of Erlang Temple Cai Family Garden Yanling Lane Gong Alley in this city. In the application form, the owner was listed as the Japanese Saito Risuke, and Wu Zhilian identified himself as Saito's agent. Regarding the owner's certificate, there was only one land lease contract signed by Wu Zhilian and Saito. The lessee in the contract was also Wu Zhilian, who was the lessee as an agent. In addition, there was a certificate from the Japanese Consulate. After verification, inquiries were made with residents in the vicinity, who stated that the Japanese had been given this land by Qi Xieyuan and Wang Guilin many years ago. It had neither been registered with the local authorities as required nor had it been filed in accordance with Article 6 of the Provisional Regulations on the Lease of Land and Houses by Foreign Churches in the Interior promulgated by the Ministry of Internal Affairs in the 17th year of the Republic of China. Wu Zhilian, as the Secretary of the Judicial Yuan, and acting as the real estate agent of a foreigner, has lost his status as a public official. The period was precisely on the day of the promulgation of the Regulations on Public Officials' Service. It is unknown what Wu Zhilian relied on to recognize the Japanese as the owner of the land and even act as both the lessee and the agent of the owner, signing a 30-year lease contract with the Japanese and immediately applying for a license to build a commercial building in the name of Heji Industrial Company. Furthermore, the Jing City Land Bureau requires people applying for land surveys to submit their deeds for verification and repeated surveys before granting clearance. However, this time, the survey of the land was based solely on the contract signed by the agent Wu Zhilian and the lessee Wu Zhilian. Because they had a certificate from the Japanese Consulate, it was recognized as representing all the legal documents and a single map was issued. From then on, the Japanese could enjoy the permanent and official ownership of the land without any recourse. This is the factual situation of the case after investigation, which is submitted along with the attachments. Wu Zhilian is the Secretary of the Judicial Yuan, but he disregarded the national land rights and the various laws and regulations on land registration and transfer, colluded with the Japanese in private, and signed a lease contract to achieve his private speculation and profit-seeking plan, which is a violation of Article 9 of the Regulations on Public Officials' Service and should be severely punished. As for Yu Shunqian, as the Director of the Bureau, how carefully should he handle the registration of land by foreigners? Now that the Japanese are not establishing a church, school, or hospital, they have no right to lease or purchase land in this capital. There is no document proving the transfer of the land they have acquired, and they have not followed the filing procedures. On what basis did the Bureau publicly recognize the Japanese as the owner and acknowledge Wu Zhilian's contract, which was managed by the agent and lessee, and did not require them to submit the contract for verification as required before issuing the map? After investigating this case, it is clear that Wu Zhilian colluded with the Japanese in private to transfer land rights, and Yu Shunqian colluded with Wu Zhilian to cheat and provide a double guarantee for the Japanese's illegal possession of land rights. Their crimes are the same, and there is no way to forgive them. It is requested that they be handed over for punishment together, and the Executive Yuan should be instructed to order the Nanjing Municipal Government to revoke the map issued by the Land Bureau and stop the issuance of licenses by the Public Works Bureau. After Liu Woqing and Yu Hongqi Gao Lu, members of the Control Yuan, were assigned to review the case, they reported that after reviewing the case, they believed that Wu Zhilian colluded with the Japanese to privately sign a lease contract and obscurely obtain land rights, which was already a violation of official regulations. Moreover, the land is in the capital. If lawless villains in the city are allowed to continue their evildoing, not only will they use their position to seek personal gain, but they will also disregard national sovereignty and collude with foreigners, taking advantage of the law to seek honor and cause foreign troubles. As for Yu Shunqian, Director of the Jing City Land Bureau, he only relied on a certificate from the Japanese and did not carry out the procedures for verifying the deed before issuing the map. If he was not colluding with Wu Zhilian to seek profits, he was disregarding the law and betraying his duties. It is requested that they be handed over for punishment together in accordance with the law, and the Executive Yuan should be requested to instruct the Municipal Government to immediately revoke the map and stop the issuance of licenses to prevent disputes. This case involves high-ranking officials seeking personal gain, betraying national rights, and should be requested to be severely punished as a warning to others."

Red Bandits Slaughter and Wash Out Shicheng County, Jiangxi Province 45

People's Militia Fought Bloodily with Red Bandits for Months

Many Small Villages Were Destroyed and Many People Died

A telegram from Nanchang reports: Shicheng is located in a remote area on the border of Jiangxi and Fujian, bordering Ruijin, Yudu, and Tinghang. The folk customs are fierce and the best in the province. Therefore, the county's people's militia is known for its bravery and skill in battle. Small groups of Red Bandits are often defeated by them. However, after Zhu Mao Peng suffered heavy losses at Gaoshengxu in Xingguo last year, they fled to the area of Shicheng, Ruijin, Yudu, Tingzhou, Liancheng, and Ninghua, and held a fake National Soviet Representative Congress in the mountains of Shicheng. At that time, Zhu Mao's main force was concentrated in the three counties of Shi, Rui, and Ting. The county seat had already been captured by them. The people's militia in various parts of Shicheng retreated to the various mountain villages and earth forts, relying on the dangers to defend to the death. Refugees helped the old and carried the young, following like ants attached to a document. However, the Red Bandits coveted the people's militia's guns and hated their anti-communism so much that they would not be satisfied unless they were obtained. Therefore, Shicheng was slaughtered and washed out by the Red Bandits. Recently, I met a gentleman who escaped from Shi to the province. According to him, the entire territory of Shicheng is mountainous, and transportation is extremely inconvenient. The Red Bandits always wanted to occupy it as a bandit's nest. Fortunately, the people's militia worked hard to suppress them, so the entire county has not yet been communized. In September of last year, Zhu Mao again sent Peng Dehuai's fake Fourth Army and Lin Biao's fake Eleventh Army and Luo Binghui, by Ruijin attacked Shicheng in an attempt to eliminate the people's militia and absorb their guns. At that time, there were seven mountain villages and eleven earth forts in the county. The people's militia fought bloodily with them for months, until their ammunition was exhausted and reinforcements were cut off, and they were successively lost. Only the two mountain villages of Hongshi and Yunjing, which are known for their steepness, were still able to protect refugees from Yudu, Ruijin, Ningdu, and Ninghua, and were mostly inhabited inside. The defenses were extremely strong, and the food supply was also prepared in sufficient quantities, estimated to last for two years. However, the Communists still launched a full-scale attack. In December, the Ningdu rebel soldiers joined the fake Fourth Army, and on the morning of New Year's Day this year, they continuously fired several heavy artillery pieces at the village, as densely as a string of firecrackers. Several shells hit the village gate, destroying the city walls and burning the houses. Later, the earth nitrate caught fire, making it impossible to approach, and the entire village was burned down. More than half of the villagers died, and the entire village was lost. After the bandits entered the village, they killed everyone they met, and the corpses piled up like mountains. They also seized more than 200 rifles, dozens of Mauser pistols, and more than ten sedan guns, losing property worth millions of dollars. Huang Guanying, a member of the Party and Government Committee, and more than 1,700 civilians were all bound. Recently, the bandits have become more violent due to the loss of the two villages, burning and killing everywhere, and washing everything away. Therefore, the number of refugees fleeing the county is increasing day by day, with tens of thousands of people displaced in Lichuan, Qingliu, Jianning, and Ninghua, without clothing or food, dying and looking at each other in extremely tragic conditions. (January 21)

Liu Guitang's Troops Departed from Wenkou 46

Jinan Telegram: Han Fuqu sent Senior Advisor Cheng Xixian as his plenipotentiary representative on the 23rd, along with Aide-de-Camp Director Meng Guangshan, transporting 1,300 sets of military uniforms along with Liu Guitang's representatives Xia Ziming and Li Ziming, etc., to Da Wenkou by special train, to meet with Liu Guitang, and negotiate the date of departure. They arrived at Wenkou at 6:30 PM. Xia Ziming first conveyed to Liu the intentions of Han's dispatch of Cheng and others to Wenkou, saying that Chairman Han was unable to finish making the military uniforms in time, so he first brought 1,300 sets, and the rest would be made later. He only hoped to depart as soon as possible to Gaotang, the designated location. If everyone had any doubts, Cheng Commander (i.e., Cheng Xixian) could be ordered to depart with the train as a guarantee, and so on. Liu said that it was not impossible for his troops to depart by train, but Guo Mafeng, Yin Shigui, Yin Shixi, and others were going out of the mountains for the first time and were inevitably suspicious. This matter still had to be discussed with them. That night, Liu Guitang, Guo Mafeng, Yin Shigui, Yin Shixi, and others held a meeting. All the leaders were willing to depart by train, but the soldiers were still inevitably suspicious, so it was decided to depart by both train and on foot to save face on both sides. Liu Guitang, Guo Mafeng, Yin Shigui, Yin Shixi, and others led Liu's troops, Liu Huaizhi's Second Regiment, and those who were not wearing military uniforms on foot, departing from Da Wenkou on the morning of the 25th, staying overnight in Xiazhang (40 li), the next day staying overnight in Feicheng (50 li), the third day passing through Wangzhaodian (15 li) and Zhangjiadian (20 li) and staying overnight in Shuili Pu (30 li), the third day crossing the Yellow River from Pingyin and staying overnight in Huguantun (60 li), the fifth day passing through Xingzhai (50 li) and Yangguantun (15 li) and arriving in Gaotang (20 li). From Gaotang, they would then gather at Yaozhan. Liu's First Regiment, Wu Lianjie's troops, and those wearing military uniforms from other units, along with office staff, would depart north on two trains on the morning of the 25th, passing through Jinan to Yucheng and Beizhangzhuang to get off the train and go to Yaozhan to gather. This morning, this plan was communicated to Cheng Xixian, who agreed to return to Jinan to convey it to Chairman Han. At 2:00 PM, Cheng took the original train back to Jinan and reported to the Provincial Government. Han heard that Han could agree to this matter and it was resolved. Two empty trains departed from Tai'an to Da Wenkou today to prepare for transportation. (January 24)

Jinan Continued Telegram: Liu Guitang's troops, who had been stranded in Da Wenkou for two weeks, were completely resolved after Cheng Xixian's visit to Wenkou. This morning (the 25th), they all departed from Da Wenkou in two groups. Liu Guitang, Guo Wensheng, Yin Shi, and others led those who were walking first, with no more than a quarter of them wearing military uniforms and civilian clothes. After the pedestrians departed, those taking the train boarded the train with national flags inserted. The first train, led by Liu's Aide-de-Camp Director Chen Yide, departed at 8:00 AM. The second train, led by Liu's First Regiment Commander Wu Lianjie and Aide-de-Camp Zhang Jingjing, departed at 8:30 AM. The first train arrived in Jinan at 1:50 PM, and the second train arrived in Jinan at 1:30 PM. Cheng Xixian, a senior hall official sent by Han, arrived at the station, issued living expenses, and gave a brief speech, urging them to pay for their purchases along the way and not to harass the local area. At 2:20 PM, the first train departed, and at 3:00 PM, the second train departed, leaving Jinan to Zhangzhuang to get off the train and go to Yaozhan to gather. It is reported that after Liu's troops arrive in Gaotang, Han will send Cheng Xixian to Yaozhan to check their guns and numbers in order to reorganize them into a division and give them a title. (January 25)

Jiangsu Chambers of Commerce Initiate the Organization of the Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce 47

The chambers of commerce of Zhenjiang, Wuxian, Wujin, Jiangdu, and other counties previously requested the Provincial Party Department to approve the organization of the Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce. On the 20th of this month, they were informed that the consent of more than two-thirds of the province must be obtained, the procedures must be completed, and personnel would be sent to guide them. It is now heard that the original initiators of the request for organization were the 35 chambers of commerce of Zhenjiang, Wuxian, Yixing, Liyang, Xinghua, Wujin, Luhe, Qingpu, Jiangdu, Danyang, Tongshan, Wujiang, Wuxi, Gaochun, Jiangyin, Haimen, Pixian, Yizheng, Chongming, Kunshan, Xiaoxian, Taixian, Donghai, Taicang, Huaiyin, Gaoyou, Yancheng, Baoying, Hushu, Sishui, Shengze, Zhenze, Guazhou, Shuangcha District, and Jinle District. The 24 chambers of commerce of Changshu, Suqian, Qidong, Huaian, Nantong, Jingjiang, Guanyun, Songjiang, Chuansha, Jiading, Lishui, Suining, Taixing, Nanhui, Minhang Yilin, Xiannvzhen, Nanxiang, Jiangzhen, Yiling, Shaobo, Jurong Jiu District, Shi'erxu, and Lvsi District agreed to this organization. There are 42 county chambers of commerce and 17 town chambers of commerce, totaling 59. The number of legally established chambers of commerce on file with the Department of Industry and Commerce has exceeded two-thirds. The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce is now reporting to the Provincial Party Department, requesting the issuance of a permit and the dispatch of personnel for guidance. As for the preparations for the Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, in February of last year, when representatives of the county chambers of commerce came to Zhenjiang to discuss the business tax, they had already recommended the chambers of commerce of Zhenjiang, Jiangdu, Nantong, Tongshan, Wuxian, Wuxi, Changzhou, Wujiang, and Gaoyou to take charge. Once the instructor from the Provincial Party Department is appointed and the permit is issued, a preparatory meeting will be convened to draft the articles of association, and then a general meeting will be held to elect officers.

Wuhu Quick Telegram 48

Chen Tiaoyuan, due to the urgent need for military pay for his troops, specially sent personnel to Wuhu yesterday, instructing Li Gengchang, the Wuhu Customs Superintendent, to temporarily allocate 50,000 yuan from the customs revenue to meet the urgent needs. If this cannot be done, then personnel will have to be sent to the customs to collect it. Superintendent Li and Wuhu Customs Commissioner Iida Taro have separately telegraphed the Ministry of Finance and the Inspector General of Customs, requesting instructions for handling the matter.

Here, due to the diplomatic relations, the military and police are intensifying their vigilance over local security. Since yesterday, they have been implementing checks on pedestrians every night. After the Shanghai incident, the anti-Japanese attitude of the schools became even more激昂, declaring their willingness to fight the enemy with their bare hands. There is currently a Japanese warship anchored in Wuhu.

Bandits attacked Liu'an, and the county seat is in danger. In addition to ordering Yang Mingfang's 163rd Brigade stationed in Anqing to rush to suppress them, Chen Tiaoyuan yesterday added a regiment from a certain brigade to rush to assist. Hefei, being adjacent to Liu'an, is filled with fear. Local businesses here recently received a telegram stating that the gates of Hefei have been closed and pedestrians are being inspected. A large number of bandits were suddenly discovered in Xuancheng County, southern Anhui, and many villages in the surrounding areas were harassed. The various circles of the county sent representatives to Wuhu to request troops. The headquarters of the 171st Brigade stationed in Wuhu originally planned to send the machine gun company of the 341st Regiment to suppress them today, but because they received a report that the bandits had been dispersed by the people's militia, they immediately stopped. Local Telegrams

Songjiang 49

The County Government Convenes a Meeting of District Chiefs. The County Government convened a meeting of district chiefs today (28th). More than ten district chiefs, including Zhong Taishi, attended. County Magistrate Shen Yong presided over the meeting to discuss the following: (1) The County Magistrate submitted for discussion the case of how to handle the resettlement of the cadres and trainees of the security corps sent by various districts for training in Yang, who have now completed their training and returned to the original county. It was resolved that in districts that have already established a security corps, they should be given priority for appointment when squad leader vacancies arise. In districts that have not yet established one, they should be appointed as squad leaders during organization. (1) The case of the security corps cadres and trainees requesting reimbursement of travel expenses of more than 70 yuan from Yang back to their home county. It was resolved that the expenses should be shared equally by the districts. (1) The case of how to correct the collection of rice and grain by various districts to replenish the reserves, often involving the collection of fields from villages, towns, police stations, and outside districts. It was resolved that the County Government should order each district to instruct the village and town chiefs to supervise the village and town police to immediately correct such situations if they occur. Collection should be based on the location of the field in principle. (1) District Chiefs Zhong Taishi and Wang Huankun proposed the construction of the Lügang Jingzha to evenly distribute the water volume and maintain farmland. It was resolved that the County Government should consult with the Jin and Qing counties to discuss and proceed with the construction.

Wuxi 50

A Large Number of Gamblers Escorted to Court for Interrogation. Jian Xun, the chief of the Inspection Office of the Military and Police Corps Joint Patrol, and inspectors Sun Dasan led a team of soldiers on the 27th of this month and destroyed a large gambling den at No. 173 Jiangyin Lane outside the North Gate, and captured 19 gamblers, including Tang Axi, Chen Hanbao, Zhao Yougen, Jiang Xilin, Lü Lin, Zhou Aliu, Yu Fugen, Zhou Ashun, Wang Tianyuan, Wei Awu, Zhou Arong, Tang Ahong, Gu Ashun, Xu Shoupeng, Yu Xuechi, Li Axi, Feng Ronggen, Lin Aqi, and Zhou Shunbao. They were all taken to the office. Yesterday, a document was prepared and transferred to the Prosecutor's Office of the Court, where Prosecutor Du interrogated them in court and ordered them to be detained together pending sentencing.

Counter-Revolutionary Criminals Sentenced One by One. Six counter-revolutionary criminals from this county, Qin Xiangying, Qu Huimin (i.e., Jiang Zhenglin), Zhou Chousheng, Zhu Yongtai, Cai Xingquan, and Zhu Xianglin, have been detained since being arrested by the public security authorities. They have not yet been sentenced. It is now learned that the criminals have been interrogated by the provisional court and the trial has ended. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the sentencing was scheduled. County Magistrate and Presiding Judge Chen Chuande and Judges Huang and Chen were seated in the court, and after a joint trial, Qin Xiangying and Zhu Yongtai were declared not guilty and released on bail. The remaining Qu Huimin and Zhou Shousheng were each sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment. Cai Xingquan was sentenced to five years of imprisonment, and Zhu Xianglin was sentenced to one year and three months of imprisonment.

Changzhou 51

Bandits Rob Passengers. Near Luowu Bridge, north of Wuyi, on the morning of the 27th at around 2:00 AM, a night car passenger was passing by in a rickshaw when two people suddenly emerged from the riverbank, one wearing a long gown and the other wearing a gray military uniform. They ordered the rickshaw to stop, stepped forward to search, and showed a handgun to intimidate. They then robbed all the silver dollars they had with them. Afterwards, the rickshaw puller asked the nearby police station to arrest the bandits.

Chongming 52

The Military's Road Building is Actively Underway. Since being ordered to be stationed in Chongming in December of last year, Cao Pang, the commander of the Second Regiment of the Provincial Security Corps, has spared no effort in maintaining local security and has paid particular attention to construction projects. For example, holding clearing operations, raising shares for civilian skills training centers, and organizing joint military and police offices have all been initiated by the commander in conjunction with local officials and gentry. Now, in order to fully prepare Chongyi for national defense, Commander Cao has also presented a proposal to the provincial government to conduct military road construction, which commenced on the 21st of this month, from Chongming County to Xinkai River. The road is about 30 li long and is scheduled to be completed in ten days. About sixteen Hua Li have been built and it is expected to be completed by the end of this month.

Nantong 53

Punishment Measures for Bandit Suppression in Bandit Suppression Areas. The Higher Court, in consultation with the Provincial Government Pacification Headquarters, has designated Nantong, Rugao, and 25 other counties as bandit suppression areas. A provisional court has been specially established for Red Bandit cases to try and punish them in accordance with the Emergency Law on Punishing Those Who Harm the Republic of China. Non-bandit suppression areas should be returned to the Higher Court for trial.

Deployment in Various Ports Along the Yangtze River and the Sea. The troops stationed along the Yangtze River and the sea in Jiangbei Tonghai, as well as the navy, have been ordered to set up defenses strictly, and infantry and artillery teams have been sent to guard each port in order to avoid accidents.

The First Batch of Iron-Blooded Army Departs. The National Salvation Volunteer Corps of Tongyi has organized the Iron-Blooded Army. The first team, including Xu Huanxin, left Tong on the 28th to go north.

The Sea Bandits in Sanjia Town are Becoming More Rampant. Sanjia Town has been occupied by a large group of sea bandits from Haizhou. Recently, due to a lack of food and supplies, they have been looting the surrounding villages on a large scale. They demand food and firewood before negotiating ransoms for kidnapped victims. The bandits are particularly harsh in extorting fishermen, and their power is becoming more rampant.

Zhenjiang 54

The Notorious Bandit Su Fangzhi of Qiaotou is Arrested. The notorious bandit Su Fangzhi of Qiaotou Town in the county has been acting lawlessly in the area, has many followers, and is often in contact with bandits, making it difficult for the people of the area to sleep peacefully. The people have repeatedly reported the facts to the Third Regiment. The regiment commander, upon hearing the report, immediately dispatched a team to arrest Su on the 19th of this month. After Su was arrested, his followers spread rumors that if the gentry did not guarantee him, they would lead bandits to burn and kill. The people in the area were shocked upon hearing this. Yesterday, someone came to the province to request bail from the regiment headquarters.

Yangzhou 55

The Zhenjiang Yangzhou Automobile Ferry is Robbed by Bandits. At 5:30 PM on the 27th, the Zhenjiang Yangzhou Automobile Company's ferry "Xinzhenjiang" was sailing from Zhen to Liuxu when six or seven bandits suddenly appeared halfway, one of whom was the leader, wearing a military uniform, speaking in a Chu-Yue accent. Three bandits held Mauser pistols, and the rest held daggers. They ordered the helmsman to sail east of Jiaoshan, and searched the passengers one by one for two hours. They ordered the ship to dock at Tushan Pass to land, but because the water was shallow, they ordered it to return and searched again, and changed the passengers' leather coats and overcoats. They threw the similar military uniforms into the middle of the river. When the ship was sailing near Jianbi, an oil tanker came head-on, and the bandits ordered the oil tanker to dock next to the ferry, jumped onto the oil tanker, and left. In this incident, passengers lost cash of about 10,000 yuan or more. Zhao, a quartermaster from the Supervisory Office, who had collected 3,000 yuan from the capital, was also robbed, and one passenger had a diamond ring worth about 5,000 yuan robbed.

Qingjiang 56

Martial law is implemented in Haizhou. Liu Guoming, Brigade Commander of the 32nd Division stationed in Haizhou, believes that due to the tense diplomatic situation and Haizhou being a key commercial area and an important coastal location, considerable measures must be taken to prevent unexpected incidents. Therefore, the following five specific martial law regulations are stipulated: (1) Martial law hours are from 10:00 PM to 6:00 AM the next day. (2) During martial law hours, all agencies must hold a pass to pass through, except in cases of special incidents. (3) Anyone who dares to spread rumors to mislead the public or impersonate a soldier to stir up trouble during this period will be dealt with by military law. (4) Bathhouses, teahouses, and theaters must not allow idlers to stay at night. (5) Lodgings and hotels should report any suspicious persons to the military law office of the Brigade Headquarters; violators will be punished.

Xinghua 57

The Red Cross distributes cotton clothing. Mr. Yang Meng'ang, a member of the Xinghua Red Cross branch, solicited donations in Shanghai from philanthropist Fang Jiyang, who donated a total of 258 sets of cotton-padded jackets, trousers, and clothing of various sizes for disaster relief in Xinghua. These items have already been transported to Xinghua and distributed. In addition, the branch received 250 sets of winter relief cotton-padded jackets, trousers, and clothing allocated by the general affairs office of the general association, which have also been transported to Xinghua and distributed. The branch has submitted the clothing ticket stubs to the general association for verification and has sent separate letters of thanks.

Tunxi 58

The bandit situation and defense in the Wuyuan area. The Communist bandits led by Fang Shaozhou and Tang in the Gan-Northeast region are being jointly suppressed by the troops of Chiang, Dai, and Tang. The majority of the bandits have retreated to the vicinity of Yiyang Hengfeng Black Wind Cave, relying on the terrain for defense. The remaining scattered bandits and local Communists are causing disturbances in Leping, Dexing, Yiyang, Yujiang, and the border areas of Wuyuan. Recently, Huitian Ferry, 40 li from Leping County, was once occupied by bandit troops, who burned houses and looted people. The troops stationed in Leping under Ruan's command rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm, and the bandits retreated. Scattered bandits often infiltrate and plunder the borders of Yutan Caomen in Wuyuan and Haikou in Dexing. Although the Dexing border towns of Datiancai, Nuanshui, Raierdun, and the newly built Haikou all have stationed troops to prevent bandits, the bandits often attack just a few miles from the stationed troops, causing the bandit suppression forces to be exhausted and unable to defend effectively. Regarding the tickets seized in the rural areas of Wucheng earlier, except for three members of the self-defense corps who were released, the rest are still detained by the bandits. It is said that the Catholic priest was asked for 100,000 yuan, and Section Chief Yu of the county government was asked for 40,000 yuan. According to the released self-defense corps members, they were released in Hengfeng and given a pass by the bandits, sent to Village A by people from Village A, then to Village B by people from Village B, and then to Village C by people from Village C, stopping just before reaching Wuyuan. All along the way, there are existing agencies. The defense of Wucheng is still guarded by the camp of Han Changchuan. Recently, two more companies and mortars have been transferred from Huaqiao in Dexing to Wuyuan to strengthen its forces. The newly appointed magistrate of Wuyuan, Ke Kaiyun, has also come to Wuyuan to take office and has received 100 guns and 50 newly organized police officers from the provincial government to aid in defense. Therefore, public morale has been stabilized.

Local News

Japanese Troops Attacked the Chinese Area Last Night 59

Our Troops Defended Themselves Justifiably

A Conflict Occurred Between Both Sides

The Municipal Government Notified All Consulates

And Protested to the Japanese Consulate

The Authorities of the Chinese and Foreign Concessions

Both Declared Martial Law Yesterday

Last night, serious news spread from the foreign side. At 12:00 AM last night, Japanese marines attacked Zhabei. Initially, at 11:10 PM, a small squad of several dozen Japanese marines set out from the headquarters at the end of North Sichuan Road to Tiantong'an, first occupying Tiantong'an Station. The station staff immediately left, but at this time, our 19th Route Army stationed in Zhabei remained quietly defending the line and did not fire. Around 12:00 AM, the Japanese marines used Tiantong'an Station as a base and launched attacks on our army's defense line in several squads. Our stationed troops believed that the conflict was initiated by the other side and had no choice but to resist, immediately rising up to fight. As such, Shanghai, where all parties were trying to ease tensions, suddenly became a state of war. The battle situation investigated on the ground by our reporter is recorded below:

Tiantong'an Station: At 11:10 PM last night, a small squad of about several dozen Japanese marines, all carrying portable machine guns, riding motorcycles, and wearing white cloths on their arms, were led into Tiantong'an Station by plainclothes Japanese. At this time, the station staff all avoided the conflict and left. Our troops mostly scattered and lay in wait, quietly defending the line and remaining extremely calm.

Zhabei Street Fighting: Around 11:00 PM last night, Japanese marines in the Tiantong'an area first opened fire on our 19th Route Army defense forces with several rifle shots, and then charged towards our army's defense line on both sides of the Songhu Railway and Qiujiang Road. Our soldiers were extremely angry and displayed immense courage, using machine guns to fire. The Japanese army charged several times, but were repelled by our army. After this, both sides resisted with rifles. Until 12:50 AM, the Japanese army supplemented their forces from the rear and launched a fierce attack on our army. Our army fought back with all its might, and after fighting each other until 1:20 AM, the Japanese army still failed and retreated to the east of Tiantong'an. During the fierce battle between the two sides, the sound of machine guns never stopped. According to foreign sources, the Japanese army suffered heavy losses during the charge. From 1:30 AM onwards, the sound of gunfire became less frequent and gradually moved eastward towards Tiantong'an, presumably due to the Japanese army's retreat. However, at 1:50 AM, the sound of machine guns started again, and was very dense. The flashes of bullets could be seen on the roof of Songhu Station. The fierce battle continued until 2:30 AM, and the gunfire had not yet stopped. At the same time, more than a dozen gunshots were heard at the Baoshan Road intersection, and more than a dozen gunshots were also heard in the North Station area. The lights inside the station also went out immediately. At this time, the densest gunfire seemed to be between Qiujiang Road and Songhu Station. However, when the reporter left the vicinity of North Station at 2:40 AM this morning, the gunfire was less frequent again.

Contact at Jiangwan: After the Japanese army provoked at Tiantong'an Station, at the same time in Jiangwan, Japanese marines also made contact with the 6th Regiment of our 78th Division. Initially, there was only a conflict between sentries. For the sake of justifiable defense, our army immediately actively fought back. The Japanese army charged several times, but were repelled by our army. Our army's morale was high, and everyone fought with the strength of ten men. The battle continued until this newspaper went to press, and the Japanese army ultimately failed.

The Front Line Did Not Move: According to the latest news from this newspaper, as of 4:00 AM this morning, as a result of our army's brave fight, the front line had not moved at all. Our army captured three Japanese armored vehicles and destroyed one. Both sides suffered casualties.

Sudden Fire: At 2:40 AM this morning, while the two sides were engaged in a fierce battle, a large fire suddenly broke out north of Laobazi Road and Fuxing Road, and south of Tiantong'an Station. For a time, the fire was blazing, and the situation was huge. Because the area was in the war zone, the fire had not been extinguished by 3:50 AM.

Bombing Wusong: At around 10:00 PM last night, thirteen Japanese warships sailed into Sanjia Water and bombarded the Wusong Fort, firing thirty to forty shells. Our army initially actively fought back, but then suddenly became silent. The Japanese warships thought that the fort had been destroyed, and were about to land and occupy it, when our fort suddenly opened fire again, and the Japanese warships retreated slightly. After that, news between Shanghai and Wusong suddenly stopped, and the battle situation in Wusong is yet to be reported.

Headquarters News: According to news released by the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, the Japanese naval commander stationed in Shanghai suddenly issued an emergency ultimatum to the Chinese authorities last night, ordering them to withdraw the Chinese troops from Zhabei to a suitable location at night. While our country's authorities were holding a meeting to discuss measures, the Japanese marines in the Qiujiang Road area of Zhabei had already clashed with Chinese soldiers, and gunshots suddenly rang out. As of 12:10 AM this morning, the telephone lines in Zhabei were completely cut off, and the telephone bureau staff had all fled. Even the Chinese and foreign telephone lines directly connecting to Zhabei were all cut off.

Sudden Rise of Aircraft: At 4:30 AM this morning, suddenly an aircraft flew from east to north and then to the southwest for aerial reconnaissance. At 4:45 AM, it turned again to fly towards Pudong, and then shuttled back and forth in the airspace of the concession for reconnaissance. It was still soaring in the sky when this newspaper went to press.

Important Proclamations from the Municipal Government 60

The Municipal Government Notifies Consuls of All Countries: The Municipal Government sent a letter to the consuls general of all countries stationed in Shanghai, stating: "Greetings. Regarding the recent Sino-Japanese negotiations, in order to seek a peaceful resolution and maintain the peace and stability of this city, the mayor has fully accepted the four conditions proposed by the Japanese consul general, and has replied to the Japanese consul general in a letter at 1:45 PM today, expressing satisfaction. Unexpectedly, at 11:25 PM this evening (28th), the Municipal Public Security Bureau received an envelope from the Japanese consul general, containing two announcements from the commander of the First Overseas Fleet of Japan to the mayor and the director of the Public Security Bureau, stating that the Imperial Navy, in view of the fact that many Japanese nationals reside in the Zhabei area, intends to deploy troops there to maintain order and take responsibility for security. The commander hopes that the Chinese side will promptly withdraw all Chinese troops and their hostile facilities from the Zhabei area. Subsequently, at 12:00 AM that same night, the Municipal Public Security Bureau received a report from Zhabei that the Japanese marines had begun free military action in the area and were attacking the Chinese area. The Japanese consul general has already replied to the municipal government, expressing satisfaction, but the Japanese navy has suddenly taken this kind of military action, which is quite astonishing. All responsibilities for disrupting peace and hindering the peace and stability of this city shall be borne by the Japanese side. In addition to lodging a serious protest with the Japanese consul general, a corresponding letter is sent to you, asking you to investigate and uphold justice and friendship. This is addressed to the consuls general of the United Kingdom (John Brenan), France (Kocklin), the United States (Edwin S. Cunningham), and Italy (Fonderich) stationed in Shanghai."

The Municipal Government Lodges a Serious Protest with the Japanese Consul: The Municipal Government sent a letter of protest to the Japanese consul general, stating: "Greetings. Regarding the recent Sino-Japanese negotiations in this city, in order to seek a peaceful resolution, the mayor has accepted the four conditions proposed by your consul general, and a reply was sent at 1:45 PM this afternoon (28th). At that time, your consul general expressed satisfaction. Unexpectedly, at 11:25 PM this evening, the Municipal Public Security Bureau received an envelope from your consulate general, containing an announcement from the commander of the First Overseas Fleet of Japan to the mayor and the director of the Public Security Bureau, stating that the Imperial Navy, in view of the fact that many Japanese nationals reside in the Zhabei area, intends to deploy troops there to maintain order and take responsibility for security. The commander hopes that the Chinese side will promptly withdraw all Chinese troops and their hostile facilities from the Zhabei area. Your consul general has now deemed the mayor's reply satisfactory, but your country's navy has suddenly taken this military action, which is quite astonishing. All responsibilities for disrupting peace and for any incidents that may occur in this city shall be borne by your side. The mayor hereby lodges a serious protest, requesting that you forward this to your country's navy and promptly cease military action, so as to avoid further escalation of the situation, and hopes to hear back from you. This is addressed to Murai Kuramatsu, the consul general of Japan stationed in Shanghai."

The Determination of Military Leaders 61

Cai Tingkai's Speech in Zhenru: The various divisions of the 19th Route Army of the National Revolutionary Army are garrisoned around the Jinghu area. Army Commander Cai Tingkai believes that the current situation is tense, and the army's responsibility for garrisoning the Jinghu area is particularly important. Therefore, at 1:00 PM yesterday, he summoned all the officers and soldiers of the 3rd Regiment of the 78th Division in Zhenru for a speech, with many sincere words, encouraging the soldiers' spirit of patriotism.

Dai Ji Expresses Justifiable Defense: The situation in this city is extremely serious. The responsibility for defending the territory lies with Dai Ji, the commander of the Songhu Garrison. A reporter from this newspaper specially went to the Longhua headquarters yesterday morning to visit Commander Dai and inquire about his attitude towards this incident. Commander Dai replied that the policy towards Japan, whether it be peace or war, should be decided quickly, and the important key lies in internal unity and the consolidation of the central government. Fortunately, Mr. Wang and Mr. Chiang have jointly entered Beijing, and the central government is responsible. As for the Shanghai incident, the troop movements are all subject to the orders of the Ministry of Military Affairs. The troops of the 78th Division of this headquarters are left under the command of Army Commander Cai Tingkai in Shanghai. Commander Dai finally said that our army will never attack others first, but if the Japanese army attacks, our army cannot but resist. Success or failure is not a consideration. If that is the case, the devastation of Shanghai will be unimaginable. He could not help but sigh.

The Municipal Government Announces Martial Law 62

Since the Japanese army has attacked our army, in addition to notifying the consuls of all countries and protesting to the Japanese consul, the municipal government must also take comprehensive consideration of the rear defense. Last night, the municipal government specially instructed the Municipal Public Security Bureau to announce special martial law, and all gatherings and associations of the public are prohibited.

The Situation in the Nanshi Area 63

Key Areas Defended

Residents Panic

Strict Defense of Gaochang Temple: The Gaochang Temple area is an important military area, so martial law is the strictest. Sacks for defense work have been set up at the entrance of the arsenal. As for the defense of the river surface in that area, from Nan Wharf to Longhua Bay, small boats patrol back and forth. Sandbags are also piled up behind the aircraft station, and the defense is extremely strict.

Precautions Taken by the Municipal Government: For thorough defense, the Municipal Government specially dispatched a police detachment from the Public Security Bureau and a platoon of police from the section chief of the Third District to deploy around the Municipal Government, both in front and behind. From 2:00 PM, it was ordered to close the gates of the Municipal Government to prevent unforeseen circumstances.

Residents Moved Out One After Another: Rumors abounded in this city yesterday. Residents in Nanshi and the walled city inquired and informed each other, all in a state of panic. From morning to noon, the general public hired vehicles to transport valuable clothing and items to the concession for storage. Families even moved out, and the roads were filled with an endless stream of people.

The Defense Corps Went Out on Duty Yesterday: Because the situation became even more serious yesterday, the Chinese area defense corps ordered all teams at 2:00 PM to immediately summon all members, fully armed, to garrison the team headquarters for preparedness. The advance guard went out earlier in the evening to strengthen the defense.

The Situation in the Zhabei Area 64

Residents Relocate

Trains Still Running

The situation in the Zhabei area yesterday morning was the same as the day before. At around 1:00 PM, because the Japanese residents in the area of Hongkou Shigaota Road and Jiangwan Road were moving their belongings into the concession, and the marines stationed in the Japanese primary school were also setting up machine guns, people were panic-stricken. Residents living in the Zhabei area rushed to avoid the conflict, some moving their entire families. As a result, the roads around Baoshan Road were filled with vehicles and pedestrians. However, there were too many vehicles and pedestrians, and obstacles were piled up on the road, so it was not possible to travel smoothly, and traffic was almost blocked. It was not until about 3:00 PM that it eased slightly. However, before long, it was learned that the concession would be under martial law after 4:00 PM, which caused another panic, and the situation was extremely chaotic for a time. Rickshaws suddenly raised their prices, but there was still more demand than supply. Until 4:30 PM, the concession closed the three iron gates at Kenenghai Road, North Henan Road, and Haining Road, and announced martial law. Later, because traffic was blocked,

A Scene of People Moving Out from Baoshan Road (Photo Taken by This Newspaper) 65

it began to settle down slightly. Shops in the Baoxing Road area closed at around 4:00 PM. Shops along Baoshan Road also began to close one after another from 5:30 PM. There were few pedestrians on the road. The Fifth District Public Security Bureau dispatched all armed police officers to patrol and maintain order. All troops piled up sandbags, and soldiers guarded all the key passes, all armed and looking out from high places, but they did not stop pedestrians, so there was no obstruction to traffic. Songhu trains continued to run as usual. Japanese marines stationed outside the headquarters on North Sichuan Road posted sentries, and twelve armed soldiers stood guard at the gate, carrying guns. Armored vehicles shuttled back and forth on the road. The shops on both sides of the street near where the Japanese soldiers were stationed closed early. The trains arriving and departing from North Station continued to run as usual. When the panic occurred, the staff of the Railway Bureau were not without panic, but the staff of the Traffic Department and the station continued to work as before. All passengers arriving in Shanghai on various trains were unable to leave the station due to the martial law in the concession. Traffic Director Zheng Baozhao discussed with foreign engineer Desford, and then negotiated with the Commercial Corps Headquarters of the Concession, allowing passengers to enter the concession with the platform tickets of the railway. All the iron gate areas were guarded by teams from the International Commercial Corps.

The Situation in the Public Concession 66

Martial Law Declared

Defense Areas Divided

In view of the tense situation in this city, the Public Concession's Bureau of Works repeatedly negotiated with the naval commanders of the United Kingdom and the United States on defense measures, and yesterday ordered the mobilization of the British and American marines and the International Commercial Corps, who were all to go out on duty. The Board of Directors of the Bureau of Works also decided at noon yesterday to declare martial law. As for whether traffic will be cut off at night, the Board of Directors will decide this afternoon. The situation is recorded below:

Martial Law Declared in the Evening: The Director-General of the Bureau of Works issued a proclamation of martial law yesterday, which read: "The Bureau of Works of the Shanghai Public Concession, by proclamation of martial law, in accordance with its legal powers, hereby declares martial law from 4:00 PM on Thursday, January 28, 1932, and will immediately take necessary measures to maintain peace and order within the concession. This is hereby proclaimed for public knowledge. Director-General Zhong Si."

The Military Strength of Various Countries Stationed in Shanghai: According to the Mainland News, the naval and land forces of various countries stationed in Shanghai are as follows: Japan has ten warships and 1,450 marines in Shanghai. In addition, there are seventeen warships in the Yangtze River, seven warships on the northern coast of Shanghai, and three warships on the southern coast, for a total of thirty-four ships. The United States has one warship, 1,159 marines, and 53 officers in Shanghai. In addition, there are eight warships in the Yangtze River, one warship on the northern coast, and seven warships on the southern coast, for a total of fifteen ships. The United Kingdom has three warships, 2,170 soldiers, and 100 officers in Shanghai. In addition, there are seven warships in the Yangtze River and one warship on the northern coast, for a total of eleven ships. Italy has two warships in Shanghai and one in the Yangtze River. France has two warships in Shanghai, 1,002 soldiers, and 30 officers. In addition, there are three warships in the Yangtze River. The United States has 39 warships of various types stationed in the Philippine Islands. Its fast destroyers and the Houston, the flagship of its Asian fleet, can reach Shanghai in 48 hours.

Foreign Troops Stationed in Shanghai Awaiting Orders: At 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon, the troops of the United Kingdom, the United States, and Japan stationed in Shanghai were stationed in various sections of the Public Concession according to the defense plan set several months ago. The Shanghai Commercial Corps also went out on duty and will guard the central area of the Public Concession. Patrols and special patrols from various police stations were also ordered to gather at 4:00 PM to await orders. The warships of the United Kingdom, Italy, and France in the Huangpu River were also on alert, and soldiers were not allowed to go ashore on leave.

Division of Defense Areas Within the Concession: When the Bureau of Works held a meeting yesterday morning, military officers and commanders from the United Kingdom, the United States, France, Italy, and Japan all attended. British Army Commander Freyming stationed in Shanghai was publicly elected as the commander-in-chief of the defense forces of the Shanghai Public Concession. According to the assigned defense areas, British soldiers will guard the Hongqiao defense line, the US 4th Marine Regiment will guard the section of Haig Road and Suzhou Creek, the Japanese marines will guard Hongkou (North District) and Yangshupu (East District), and the Shanghai Commercial Corps will defend the central area from the Huangpu River to Haig Road. Patrols and special patrols from various police stations will assist the army in guarding the iron gates and defensive structures.

Foreign Residents Living Outside the Chinese Area Move Into the Concession: British, American, and Portuguese residents living outside the concession have been ordered by their respective consuls general to prepare to move into the concession immediately, or to move in at a time of emergency, depending on their own assessment of the situation. However, many of those who are cautious have already moved in. As for the Japanese residents outside the concession, they have almost all moved out.

The Blue Cross Society Organizes a Rescue Team: Mr. Zhang Deyi, the director of the Qianyi Traumatic Surgery Hospital of the Chinese Blue Cross Society, in view of the urgency of the situation in recent days and because it is located at the junction of the Chinese and foreign concessions, specially organized a rescue team to be prepared for use.

The Situation in the French Concession 67

The French Concession's preparations yesterday were extremely serious. The situation is recorded below:

The Two Concessions Decide to Cooperate: Yesterday, the Bureau of Works of the Public Concession held an emergency meeting to decide on the security of the concession and decided to implement martial law. At the same time, the Board of Directors of the French Concession also convened a meeting and decided to cooperate with the Public Concession and take unified action.

Preparing Iron Mesh and Wooden Frames: Considering the tense situation in Shanghai and the importance of defense, the French authorities, starting yesterday afternoon, in addition to closing the iron gates, also hired many temporary workers and used trucks to send iron wire mesh and wooden frames to the main intersections of the areas bordering the British and French Concessions in batches. If necessary, these obstacles will be placed at the intersections to block traffic.

Closing the Iron Gates in Various Places: The French Concession authorities specially stepped up defense at noon yesterday. The iron gates at the various places where the Chinese and French Concessions bordered each other were all closed, leaving only a side door on the pedestrian path for pedestrians to travel back and forth. However, the iron gates at No. 16 Pier in Nanshi and Xinkai River were not closed, so that vehicles could enter and exit at these two places. In an instant, vehicles were extremely crowded. The trams running back and forth along the Republic Road were also blocked by other vehicles, and more than a dozen trams in total were stopped one after another at the Xinkai River Station. The other tram lines, Route 5 and Route 6, were temporarily shortened and turned around at the Xiaobeimen iron gate. In each police station, the police stations under their jurisdiction dispatched more than a dozen armed Chinese, Western, and Vietnamese police officers to guard each station, and sent detectives to patrol in sections.

A Scene of People Moving Out at the Border Between the Chinese and French Areas (Photo Taken by This Newspaper) 68

The Municipal Government Sent an Ultimatum to the Japanese Consul Yesterday Afternoon 69

Mayor Wu Expressed Deep Sorrow

The Municipal Government sent a reply to the Japanese consul yesterday, stating: "In reply to your letter of January 20, which stated that five Japanese monks, including Tianqi, Mizukami, and followers Goto, Kuroiwa, and Fujimura, were beaten and injured near Mayushan Road on the afternoon of the 18th of this month, and proposed four conditions for acceptance. Upon receiving this, I have investigated the matter, which is unfortunate. The mayor expresses his deep regret. After receiving the report that day, considering that the case involved injury and there were clear provisions in the law, the Public Security Bureau was immediately ordered to arrest the murderers within a time limit and bring them to justice. The mayor is also willing to provide appropriate medical and consolation money to the victims to show his sympathy. As for the matter mentioned in your letter regarding the suppression of the anti-Japanese movement, it has now been found that the anti-Japanese salvation committees in various circles of the city have engaged in excessive and illegal acts. The competent authorities have been ordered to abolish the associations in order to maintain the rule of law. Regarding such excessive and illegal acts, the mayor will continue to uphold the spirit of the rule of law and order their suppression. The bureau has also been ordered to abolish other anti-Japanese groups accordingly. This letter is sent to you for your information."

The Municipal Government's reply to the Japanese protest letter was issued at 1:45 PM yesterday afternoon. Reporters visited Mayor Wu that afternoon to inquire about the reply. Mayor Wu's attitude was sorrowful, and he remained silent for a long time without saying a word. Then, with decisive and solemn words, he expressed a few words to the reporters as follows: "I am a public servant of Shanghai, and the responsibility for the safety of this city is extremely important and rests on my shoulders. Therefore, I will not hesitate to sacrifice myself to seek the safety of Shanghai. Honor, disgrace, praise, or blame are of no consideration." Mayor Wu continued, saying that he did not wish to make any further comments regarding this case in the future.

The Public Safety and Social Affairs Bureaus Ordered to Close Anti-Japanese Associations 70

Offices and Warehouses Were All Sealed

The Municipal Government, at 12 o'clock the night before last, ordered the Public Safety and Social Affairs Bureaus to jointly seal up the All-Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association. The details are as follows:

Joint Sealing: City Public Safety Bureau Chief Wen Yingxing and City Social Affairs Bureau Chief Mai Chaochu, after receiving the Municipal Government's order to abolish the All-Circles Anti-Japanese Association, each dispatched section members at 0:30 AM yesterday morning to jointly seal up (1) the executive committee of the All-Circles Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association located within the Tianhou Palace in the Fifth District, the Zhabei Inspection Sub-office on Zhongxing Road in Zhabei, and the warehouse; (2) the Caojiadu Inspection Sub-office on Jessfield Road in the Sixth District, and the warehouse on Avenue du Capitaine Belliard; (3) the Zhaojiabang Road Inspection Sub-office in the Second District, and the warehouse at No. 6 Liangyi Lane; (4) the Tanziawan warehouse in the Third District; (6) the Wusong Inspection Sub-office and warehouse in the Seventh District. The personnel of the offices were ordered to move out, and the front and back doors were locked and pasted with a "Shanghai Public Safety Bureau Seal, Month ○○" notice. This was completed at 5:00 AM.

Reporting to the Municipal Government: After the offices and warehouses of the Anti-Japanese Association were sealed, the district headquarters of the City Public Safety Bureau removed all the signboards and handed them over to the headquarters for safekeeping. Yesterday morning, the City Public Safety and Social Affairs Bureaus each submitted a report to the Municipal Government for review on the details of the joint sealing.

Futile Petition: At 9:00 AM yesterday morning, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association convened a temporary emergency meeting. It was decided to send representatives Yu Hualong, Zhang Yichen, and six others to petition the Municipal Government for immediate unsealing. The representatives then took two cars to the Municipal Government at 2:00 PM, but Mayor Wu and the Secretary-General were both away on business, and no one was in charge. They then went to Mayor Wu's private residence on Avenue Haig, but still could not meet him, and returned without success.

The Japanese Mine Warfare Fleet Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon 71

Planes Circled the Entire City Once

Arrival of Mine Warfare Unit in Shanghai: The Japanese mine warfare fleet, continuously dispatched to Shanghai, led by the cruiser "Yubari," included the 22nd Destroyer Division: "Gao Yue," "Wen Yue," "Shui Wu Yue," "Chang Yue"; the 23rd Division: "Kiku Yue," "Mi Yue," "Yu Yue," "Mochi Yue"; the 30th Division: "Kisa Yue," "Yayoi Yue," "U Yue," totaling twelve ships. The "Yubari's" captain was Saito Niro, the 22nd Division Commander was Kobata, the 23rd Division Commander was Suzuki Tayuki, and the 30th Division Commander was Hara Ikusaburo. The mine warfare unit arrived off the coast of Wusong yesterday morning, anchored first, then sent a telegram to Shanghai asking for the anchoring locations for each ship. At 4:30 PM, the "Yubari" sailed into the Huangpu River and docked at the Huangpu Wharf. The other ships of the three divisions were anchored in the 24th and 25th river sections of the Huangpu River.

Marine Landing: The "Yubari" brought 400 marines from Sasebo. After arriving at the Huangpu Wharf at 5:00 PM yesterday afternoon, the marines landed immediately and were transferred to North Sichuan Road to be stationed.

Japanese Planes Flew: The Japanese aircraft carrier "Notoro" carried an air squadron to Shanghai. Yesterday morning, after two heavy bombers were prepared on the ship, they flew around the city once at about 4:00 PM, when the mine warfare fleet entered the port, and then returned to the ship to park. In total, there are now 21 Japanese warships, 1,400 marines, and approximately 20 aircraft in Shanghai, along with fully equipped field guns and machine guns.

National Alarm Bell Society Paraded to Warn the Public 72

At about 3:00 PM, they paraded around the city area and rang the bell along the way, to alert the public to go to the national crisis together.

A Bomb Was Found at the Japanese Consulate General Yesterday Morning 77

But No One Was Hurt

The Shanghai Evening Post & Mercury reported that at 8:30 this morning (the 28th), a bomb exploded near the northeast wall of the Japanese Consulate General in Hongkou, but no one was injured, and the damage was minimal. Hu Yimin Comes to Shanghai to Negotiate the Completion of the Shanghai-Shaanxi Air Route 79

Talks on the Implementation of the Five-Year Plan in Shaanxi Province

Hu Yimin, a member of the Shaanxi Provincial Government and director of the Xi'an Pacification Headquarters Office in Beijing, came to Shanghai yesterday on official business. A reporter from the Hua Dong News Agency had the following conversation with him. According to him, Chairman Yang has also taken over the position of Pacification Director and has begun to work, commanding the troops stationed in Gansu and other provinces. The Sichuan Army's Huang Yin and other troops harassed the border of Shaanxi. According to recent telegrams, they are in Hanzhong (i.e., Nanzheng County in southern Shaanxi). Commander Yang has sent troops to resolve the matter. The military affairs of Gansu and Ningxia provinces have been pacified, and local rehabilitation is underway. Commander Ma (Hongkui)'s headquarters is currently stationed in the vicinity of Xuchang, Henan. Qinzhong has suffered from disasters for more than ten years, and the people are extremely poor. After the provincial government and others made every effort to reorganize it in 1931, production was richer than before. In one or two years, it can be restored to its original state. Starting in 1933, it is planned to implement a five-year plan, hoping that capitalists will invest in land reclamation and mining, which should be considerable. He came to Shanghai this time to contact China National Aviation Corporation about the Shanghai-Shaanxi air route, which runs from Shanghai via Hankou and Laohekou to Xi'an. Record of the Women's Temperance Association Meeting 80

Ms. Shen Gave a Painful Speech

The Women's Christian Temperance Union held its sixth meeting yesterday at the YMCA and welcomed new male and female members. Among them, Ms. Shen Fugui gave a brief speech, full of anxiety and pain. She said that the rise and fall of a country depends entirely on whether its economy is sufficient. If the people buy foreign goods regardless of whether they are necessities, how can the economy of this country be sufficient? The current economic situation in our country is extremely difficult. The only way to remedy it is for our compatriots across the country to immediately implement the use of domestic goods. At this time of tense foreign aggression, there are still many unawakened intellectuals in the party, government, industry, commerce, and academic circles who continue to buy foreign goods, thinking they are beautiful and modern, not knowing that China will perish because of them. As a member of the women's community, I joined your association in the spirit of setting an example, and I am willing to do my best to publicize to the women's community in Shanghai, and I will not stop until the women compatriots across the country are aware of using domestic goods.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Pays Attention to the Increase in Tariffs in Central Europe 81

A Telegram Is Sent to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Forward a Telegram to Various Envoys Abroad to Help Mediate

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, stating that on the 23rd of this month, the Egg Industry Association wrote that various countries in Central Europe, such as Germany, Czechoslovakia, and Austria, have been discussing increasing the tax rates on various imported goods for a long time, and it seems that it will be implemented. If Chinese eggs are included, sales will be further reduced, and the national economy and people's livelihood will be even more affected. The value of our country's purchases of German goods exceeds ten times the value of Chinese goods exported. If the export of Chinese goods decreases, the ability to purchase German goods will also decrease accordingly. There is a relationship between import and export. Sino-German relations have always been close, and it is hoped that they will support each other in commerce so that both sides can benefit and maintain international friendship. Therefore, it is in the interest of both sides for the German government not to increase the future import tax on eggs. The Association believes that an early proposal should be made, and time should not be lost. In addition to requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to quickly send a telegram to the German Embassy to first seek to cancel the tax from the German government in advance, and to send telegrams to the embassies in Vienna and Prague to exempt the import tax on Chinese eggs, they are specially requesting your Association to appeal to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to quickly find a way to stop it, so as to maintain our country's egg industry's trade with Central Europe, which would be greatly appreciated by the German envoys. The Association believes that at the present time, all countries in the world are in a state of economic depression, and increasing import tariffs in the hope of self-preservation is a common policy. However, the Far East market has always been relied upon by various countries, and countries that have been financially depleted after the European War, as well as emerging countries, want to use our Chinese market to open up their sales channels, which is especially important. It is appropriate to request a reciprocal strategy. The tariff war is not suitable for the situation. The quantity of Chinese goods imported by later countries is small, and the competition is not as fierce as that of advanced countries in Europe. Therefore, from the perspective of the interests of each country, there is no need to increase the import tax on Chinese goods. If the Ministry of Foreign Affairs can forward a telegram to various envoys abroad and help mediate the situation in a timely manner, the reversal plan is also expected. The relationship is not only about the egg industry. It seems that the argument should be based on all Chinese goods in order to be appropriate and avoid omissions. We hope that your Ministry will review and instruct. Respectfully, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Exemption of Business Tax for Silk Manufacturing Industry Approved 82

The Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association previously received a letter from the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, forwarding a letter from the Business Tax Collection Office of the Finance Bureau, stating that silk factories are listed in the silk manufacturing industry, and the tax rate is levied according to the amount of capital. They were instructed to order the silk factories to fill out the forms and report the situation. The Chairman of the Trade Association Committee, Shen Yichen, etc., according to the provisions of Article 1 of the Regulations on the Collection of Business Tax by the Ministry, stated that the silk exported by the factory has already paid ten taels of customs duties per package, and recently increased by five taels. The industry has already borne a heavy tax burden, so how can it be taxed again for the silk manufacturing industry? They repeatedly argued and requested an exemption from the tax. It is now learned that the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau has received instructions from the Municipal Government that the request for exemption from the silk manufacturing industry's business tax is in line with Item 4 of the reduction and exemption measures and should be approved. In addition to reporting to the Ministry for review and filing, they were ordered to notify them accordingly. The Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association has already received a letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, forwarding a letter from the Finance Bureau, requesting notification, and immediately recorded the letter and notified all members to check it.

Min People in Shanghai Are Enthusiastic About Hometown Autonomy 83

Declaration Issued

Fujian people in Shanghai and Beijing recently initiated the organization of the Fujian Local Autonomy Promotion Association to promote autonomy in their hometown. At 2:00 PM on the 27th, the inaugural meeting was held on the 5th floor of No. 141 Tianbao Road. Qiu Hanping was elected as chairman, and Pan Zuomin as secretary. The chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting. The members expressed their opinions, all believing that saving the hometown and saving the country should start with the development of civil rights in local autonomy. The association should be established in Shanghai, and after a considerable period of time, they will return to the province to work. Then, the simple rules and declarations were discussed and revised and passed. Then, temporary staff members were elected, including 11 directors: Li Yue, Qin Wangshan, Qiu Hanping, Ge Yuexi, Xu Hongkun, Pan Zuomin, Hong Guoxuan, Guo Zhaolin, Wu Yuwen, Gao Chongling, Yang Qingxuan; 5 alternate directors: Liang Longguang, Liu Zunguang, Chen Yaokun, Li Deguang, Lu Mengqing; 5 supervisors: Zhang Chuming, Huang Chengyuan, Yang Jun, Qiu Zansheng, Qiu Ruiqu; 2 alternate supervisors: Chen Jizhi, Li Gongchen; and designated the directors Qiu Hanping, Pan Zuomin, Hong Guoxuan, Guo Zhaolin, and Wu Yuwen, who are permanently in Shanghai, as standing directors, and Zhang Chuming, Qiu Zansheng, and Qiu Ruiqu as standing supervisors, and planned to send members to various counties in the province to organize branches to promote autonomy matters nearby. Now, the association's declaration is recorded as follows: The locality is the foundation of the country, and autonomy is the ladder of constitutionalism. Therefore, those who govern the country well must implement local autonomy so that the people can devote themselves to the public undertakings of the locality, thereby increasing their ability to handle public affairs, and then they can participate in national affairs, supervise the government, and advance the country into the ranks of constitutionalism, and bring all the people into the realm of freedom. Sun Yat-sen, the founder of the Republic of China, advocated the Three Principles of the People, and also regarded local autonomy as an essential means of training the people to exercise the four rights of election, initiation, referendum, and recall, and to assist in the formation of national politics. Therefore, the General Outline of National Construction and the Law on the Implementation of Local Autonomy clearly stipulate that the county is the unit of autonomy, and the county constitution, the provincial constitution, and the national constitution are established. Unfortunately, the legacy has been passed down, but it has not been implemented effectively. Although the rules have been established, they have not been promoted, which has made it impossible for civil rights to develop and politics has not been clear. Now, the government and the public know that without developing democracy, there is no way to ensure domestic peace and resist foreign aggression. Local autonomy urgently needs to be developed. People born in Fujian, Weisan and Zi, dare not forget to be respectful. Therefore, they organize the Fujian Local Autonomy Promotion Association, with a sincere heart, and together with their elders, brothers, sisters, and compatriots, maintain local peace and strive for autonomy, such as household registration surveys, land surveys, bandit elimination, Baojia implementation, road construction, agricultural promotion, educational popularization, and the use of four rights, will do their best to achieve results, so that local autonomous organizations become economic and political organizations to achieve the goals of civil rights and people's livelihood. Then, the mission of the association will be completed. This matter is of great importance and should rely on the strength of the people. It is hoped that the elders, brothers, sisters, and compatriots in the province and living overseas will actively participate and fight together, so that local autonomy in Fujian counties and cities can achieve good results, and the provincial constitution can promote the national constitution. Then, the country and the hometown will be fortunate. Respectfully, we declare this.

In Times of Disaster, Dry Rice Planting Should Be Promoted 89

Dry rice seeds come from Changchun and are planted like wheat. They are sown during Qingming and can be harvested in three months. Each mu can yield more than one dan of rice. Its properties are similar to glutinous rice, but it is not sticky. Last year, someone bought one dou of dry rice seeds from Harbin and sowed them in Xishan, Dongting, Wu County, in the spring of 1931 for trial planting. As a result, the rice heads were also four inches long, no different from those planted in the field, and the harvest was also abundant. During this period of disaster, the authorities and experts in agriculture and land reclamation should urgently find ways to promote it.

The Chinese Medicine Industry Held an Extraordinary Meeting 91

Denying Peony Bark Monopoly Market Price

The Pharmaceutical Industry Association convened an extraordinary meeting yesterday to discuss the case of the Chinese medicine industry opposing the monopoly of peony bark market prices. Twelve executive committee members attended, and Yongtai Fu, Heli Yuan, Yicheng, and Licheng sent representatives. President Zhan Tinghua reported on the letter from the Chinese Medicine Industry Association. After discussion, it was agreed that industry members act as agents to buy and sell for customers and cannot force mountain merchants to limit sales to certain companies, and there is no monopoly or manipulation. As for the high and low prices, the quality varies, and it is not unique to one place. The mountain merchants of this peony bark are unwilling to reduce prices and are allowed to return the original goods. The original letter to the Chinese Medicine Association stated: On the 26th of this month, it was approved that the letter No. 1 from your association opened by opposing Yongtai Fu and others' exclusive sales of peony bark, unauthorized raising of wholesale prices, and monopolizing and manipulating the market. The meeting resolved to use the Hangzhou market as the standard and stated that this Association has the responsibility to correct the ills of the industry. If we do not correct and restrain, we will request a reply from you. In light of this, Yongtai Fu and others are marketing peony bark, which is sold by mountain merchants. Mountain merchants come to Shanghai to handle goods and are willing to sell to whichever company and at whatever price they choose. It is a matter of business freedom for the mountain merchants. Industry members only have the right to buy or not buy and cannot force them to limit sales. The previous advertisement was posted by the mountain merchants and has nothing to do with industry members. Your association's letter wrongly accused Yongtai Fu and others of monopolizing and manipulating because they are acting as agents. It is too much to protect them. Correcting the ills of the industry is indeed the responsibility of this Association. If the medicine of industry members is mixed with fake medicine, endangering the lives of patients, this Association will sanction them. Now, Yongtai Fu and others are selling on behalf of customers. What are the ills and harms? Your association actually questioned and blamed the agents, Yongtai Fu and others, based on one-sided words, and rashly revealed this in the newspaper. Although it is a news report, it was also instructed by your association. Such wanton accusations are not appropriate for your close association. Your association should remedy and correct this in order to maintain good relations. Compared with your industry, the interest rate on pharmaceuticals is vastly different. Should your association's claim that the "increase in the burden on the poor and sick" be held accountable? On the 27th of this month, this Association convened Yongtai Fu and others to discuss this matter. It was agreed that the price of goods varies depending on quality, and it is impossible for prices to be the same in each place, and it is not unique to the pharmaceutical industry. The mountain merchants firmly refused to reduce the original price of peony bark. If the Chinese medicine industry thinks the price is not suitable, they can return the original goods. The letter has been approved and should be forwarded to your association for reference, and it is hoped that it will be forwarded to them accordingly.
