The Municipal First Public Cemetery Project to Be Completed Around Qingming Festival Last summer and autumn, the Shanghai Municipal Government purchased over 200 mu of land near the Jiangwan Gaojing Temple Station on Songhu Road, west side, to build the Municipal First Public Cemetery Base to facilitate the burial needs of citizens. Soon after, the municipal government ordered the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to invite bids, and a construction contractor undertook the construction. After half a year, the construction project is mostly completed. Today, passengers on Songhu Road can catch a glimpse of the Municipal First Public Cemetery's tomb base, archway, auditorium, and other buildings when passing Gaojing Temple. The cemetery project is still underway recently and is expected to be completed before the Qingming Festival. By then, the Municipal Health Bureau will take over the tomb base and prepare for citizens to claim land for burial. It is said that each tomb will occupy approximately 10 cubic feet of land. The municipal government will select a suitable location within the city after this project is completed to purchase land for building public graves. The Abducted Child Sent Back from Fujian, the Abductors Awaiting Sentencing Wu Zhangshi, a native of Anhui living at No. 15, Xialin Lane, Zhengjia Muqiao Street in the French Concession, has a six-year-old daughter, A'er, who often visited her maternal grandparents' home at No. 137 Zhengjia Muqiao Street, across the lane, and sometimes played with A'yin, the fourteen-year-old daughter of Zhang Chenshi, a woman from Luodian who lived upstairs in her maternal grandparents' home. On the afternoon of the 11th of this month at 2:00 PM, A'er was suddenly abducted by Li Jiarong, Zhang Chenshi's paramour, in collusion with Deng Fenglin, a fellow villager from Shandong, along with Chenshi's daughter A'yin, to Gaochang Temple in Nanshi. Through the introduction of Zhang's wife, she was sold to Lin Wangshi, a Fujian woman, and sent to the Jing'an warship moored there. At that time, A'yin was sent back because of her crying, but A'er was taken to Fujian. After Wu Zhangshi found out, she reported it to the French police. Detective Hang Guangfu arrested Deng and the related Fujian women, Wang Linshi and Tang Wangshi. Li Jiarong and Zhang's wife had already fled upon hearing the news. The Jing'an warship had already sailed to Fujian, making it impossible to retrieve the child. Deng and others were sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention. Zhang Chenshi and her daughter Zhang A'yin were deemed to have known about the incident but did not report it, raising suspicions of collusion, and were ordered to post bail pending further investigation. The above information has been recorded in previous reports. It is now known that the French police notified the local Naval Headquarters at the time, requesting them to telegraph the Fujian authorities to intercept the child. The headquarters complied and telegraphed the Fuzhou authorities. When the Jing'an warship entered the port, the child was found, and Lin Wangshi was arrested and transferred to Shanghai, handed over to the Naval Headquarters, and then to the French police for interrogation. Yesterday, the police sent the suspects in this case to the court for questioning. First, the police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, presented the case and prosecuted according to Article 258 of the Criminal Law. When questioned, Lin Wangshi confessed to buying A'er for 60 yuan to be her daughter. Deng Fenglin confessed that he was instigated by Li Jiarong, who was at large, to abduct his paramour's daughter A'yin first, but she refused, so he abducted the Wu family's daughter. Zhang Chenshi confessed that she learned about the abduction of the Wu family's child from her daughter and entrusted someone to report it to the Public Security Bureau the next day to arrest Deng, denying any collusion. The judge verified the confessions, announced the conclusion of the trial, and scheduled the sentencing for January 30th. The defendants were remanded in custody, and Zhang Chenshi and her daughter were detained for further instructions due to strong suspicions. The girl was first released to her family. Reader's Correspondence The Rope-Making Factory's Practices Making straw ropes was originally a handicraft and a sideline for farming families. For more than a decade, someone invented machine-made ropes, which led to a larger scale and greater output. In addition to being sold in Shanghai, as much as 10 million catties are sold to Japan each year, reportedly purchased by people in the egg industry there. This is something that Chinese people don't usually pay attention to, but it has the potential for export. There are more than 30 rope-making factories in Shanghai, with a trade association located in Fangbang Bridge. The first ones to open were Dong Fengji and Xie Ji. Larger ones include Li Da, Heng Kang, Xie Ji, Long Xiang, and Xinhua. Their addresses are mostly in Pudong and Gaochang Temple, Xie Xu Road, and Shi Qigang. The raw material for rope-making is only rice straw, mostly from Songjiang, with a market price of over one yuan per dan. Ropes are measured by the coil, with each coil weighing 12-13 catties or 15-16 catties, valued at four jiao or less. There are several grades of ropes, from third to seventh. The first and second grades are too thin and cannot bear weight, so they are not sold or made. The rope-making process is very simple: first, the straw is sorted to make it uniform in length, and then it is divided into strands of seven or eight or four or five. People twist the strands with a rope-making machine, which is operated by foot. There are horn-shaped tubes on the left and right, into which the straw is fed continuously. The single strands are twisted into double strands, and then the double strands are transferred to a circular iron frame inside the machine. By stepping on the machine and feeding the straw, 20 coils of rope can be twisted each day. The labor cost is 500 wen per dan of rope. The best rope-making machines are made by the Huang Detai Machinery Factory north of the Shanghai South City Guild Hall, with a price of 20 yuan per machine. The rice straw husks are soaked in lime water to rot them and used to make grass paper (i.e., the paper used by plasterers). This is a byproduct of the rope-making factory. Some people also use it as fuel, which is not very economical. (Ding) 92

Page 13

Educational News Important News The Ministry of Education Further Explains the Issue of Educational Associations, Designating the Anhui Provincial Department of Education to Explain Three Points The Ministry of Education, based on a report from the Anhui Provincial Department of Education regarding three points raised by the Xuyi County Educational Association requesting clarification on the issue of educational associations, instructed the department as follows: "Received the report. The requested clarifications are answered separately as follows: (1) According to the provisions of Article 14 of the Implementing Regulations of the Educational Association Law, alternate directors may attend directors' meetings, but cannot fill in for absent directors on a temporary basis; (2) If a director takes a long-term leave of absence, they should be asked to resign in accordance with the provisions of Article 25, Section 2 of the Educational Association Law, and the alternate directors should fill in sequentially; (3) When calculating the quorum for directors' meetings, only the attending directors should be counted, and alternate directors should not be included. Please take note and instruct compliance." Soochow University Shanghai Alumni Association's Letter to Students Remaining at the School The letter states: "To the students: Since the patriotic movement at the School of Arts and Sciences and Soochow Academy has caused turmoil, we have been deeply concerned. Therefore, after the incident occurred, our association sent staff to Suzhou to investigate the truth. On the 22nd of this month, an emergency meeting was convened at the Shanghai YMCA to report on the investigation in Suzhou. After a long discussion, we unanimously agreed that maintaining the school's discipline is the first priority. At the same time, the members of our association are willing to mediate from a third-party perspective and have elected Cheng Renjie, Dong Chengdao, Bei Songsun, Chen Tingrui, and Qian Baohe as representatives to proceed accordingly. We deeply sympathize with the patriotic movement of the students of our school. However, due to the patriotic movement, it has exceeded the norms, affecting studies, damaging school discipline, and causing educational bankruptcy, resulting in irreparable losses to the country. This is contrary to the original intention of saving the country, which we believe is beyond what you all initially expected. As for the school authorities' hasty actions, the measures taken may not be entirely satisfactory. However, in order to maintain school discipline, they have their own difficulties. If we were in their position, we might not have other options. On the student side, after thorough investigation, they declared the expulsion of President Yang, surrounded the faculty, organized a picket team, and restricted students' freedom, making it impossible for the school authorities to exercise their powers. As a result, the solemn academy has fallen into a state of emergency for two weeks, which we cannot agree with. The maintenance of school discipline is related to the students' character and is also the basis of the nation. If the principles are lost, how can the country stand? You all understand this very well, so we don't need to say more. Therefore, we confirm that the prerequisite for resolving this turmoil is to restore the original state of the school administration as soon as possible. Fortunately, according to the report from our association's investigator in Suzhou, the students remaining at the school no longer oppose President Yang. At the same time, the remaining students should cancel the organization of the picket team and the restrictions on students' freedom. Then, we can sincerely cooperate with each other, taking patriotism as the prerequisite. If the students in the school have any opinions on the patriotic movement, we, as members of the alumni, are willing to convey them on their behalf to achieve satisfactory results and prevent the glorious history of our school for more than 30 years from collapsing in one morning. This is what we sincerely pray for. We hope you will consider our humble opinions." The Secondary School Federation Again Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday The Shanghai Secondary School Federation held an emergency representatives' meeting at 1:00 PM yesterday afternoon to discuss the case of the Municipal Government's recognition of Japanese demands. A total of 21 school representatives attended, chaired by Hui Lingding Dezhao, and recorded by Quanzhang Yuan Yanwen. It was resolved that: (1) A telegram should be sent to the people of the whole country to unanimously reject the Japanese Consulate's demands. (2) After the meeting, the association should go to the Municipal Government to issue severe reprimands. (3) All sectors should unite in opposition. After the meeting, all the representatives went to the Municipal Government. When passing the Xiaomiaoqiao intersection, they were stopped by more than 30 armed police officers due to martial law. At that time, the representatives, filled with righteous indignation, cried and explained their intentions to the police, asking for passage. Many of the police officers were moved and reported to Secretary Guan of the Municipal Government, who approved the dispatch of two representatives to the Municipal Government. However, because it was outside office hours, no responsible personnel from the Municipal Government received them. The representatives returned to their respective schools at 7:00 PM. Wu Guanying Returns to Shanghai After Completing Studies in France Mr. Wu Guanying, a native of Zhangzhou, Fujian, graduated from Aurora University Medical School. Due to his outstanding academic performance, he was sent by the school to the doctoral program of the Paris University Medical School to continue his studies. At the same time, he also served as a doctor at the French National Hospital. Last winter, he presented his dissertation on "Delayed Response to Glucose in Diabetics" at the University of Paris, which was praised by Professors Taiker and La Deli and awarded the highest medical doctorate. The dissertation was also presented by Professors Taiker and others at the Paris National Academy of Medicine. After discussion by the researchers, it was considered satisfactory and awarded the 1932 National Medical Research Award, which is a rare honor for Chinese students. Mr. Wu has now returned to China from France and will arrive in Shanghai soon. Initiation of the Jiangxi Alumni Association There are no fewer than a thousand Jiangxi natives living in Shanghai. Meeting of the Electrical Engineering Technical Committee 93

The first executive committee meeting of the third session of the Technical Committee of the National Federation of Private Electrical Industries was held yesterday at the Federation's location at 11A Kiukiang Road. Attendees included Deng Zian, Zhuang Zhongxi, Zhao Songsen, Zhang Bogang, Zhang Qixue, Zhi Bingyuan, Shi Hongxi, Shen Sifang, Xu Dongren, and others. The meeting was chaired by Xu Dongren, with Li Wenzhi as the secretary. First, Zhi Bingyuan, Shen Sifang, and Shi Hongxi reported on the technical difficulties faced by the Changzhou, Changxing, and Zhenjiang companies, respectively, and the implementation of improvement plans, as well as methods of cooperation with the New China Engineering Company and the Chinese Engineers Company. Finally, it was resolved to issue a survey form within one month to investigate the resumes of technical personnel, the equipment of power plants, and the power generation status of private electrical companies nationwide. After receiving these survey forms, the committee will immediately begin to prepare the latest national electrical industry statistics and electrical maps, and will entrust technical experts to conduct on-site investigations by province and region, in an effort to improve the association. The association also plans to establish an introduction department to help electrical companies recruit technical personnel, it was said.

Private Counterfeit Money Printing Operation Cracked on New Zha Road 94

Counterfeit Money and Opium Seized

Three Male and Female Suspects Arrested

Bao Detective Li Baichuan of the General Inspectorate learned that someone had established a private counterfeit currency printing operation inside No. 48 Hongxiang Lane, New Zha Road, secretly printing various bank notes for sale and mixing them into circulation in the market, disrupting the financial system. He reported this to the head detective, and at 6:30 a.m. the day before, he, together with Western Detective Turner, Chinese Detective Wu Chunrong, Bao Detective Li Jincheng, and others, secretly went to the address to make arrests. Upon arriving at Hongxiang Lane, they saw that the house was a two-story building. The ground floor was a tailoring shop. The Chinese and Western detectives went straight to the second floor, where they found a woman named Cao Zhengshi from Anhui, sound asleep in bed. She was suddenly awakened and, upon seeing the detectives, immediately took out two ten-yuan banknotes from beside her and tore them up, intending to discard them. She was arrested by the detectives, and the torn pieces of paper were recovered. A search was then commenced, but nothing was found. The detectives then proceeded to the front room of the second floor, which was occupied by Liang Defu from Xuzhou and his wife, Liang Liushi. Under the mattress of their bed, the detectives found ninety-six five-yuan counterfeit banknotes, twelve ten-yuan counterfeit banknotes, and one pound of opium. The Liang couple were arrested. Then, in the back shed, a large amount of counterfeit money was found in a box, including one thousand four hundred and forty-nine ten-yuan banknotes, two thousand seven hundred and fifty five-yuan banknotes, and sixty-nine Sichuan Chongqing grain deed tax stamps. A printing press, a rolling pin, a basket of various chemicals, an electric motor, nineteen cans of printing ink, and other parts were also seized and taken to the New Zha Road Police Station. The head detective ordered them to be detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Court's Criminal Division One. Presiding Judge Zhou Hanting and Prosecutor Qian Hongye came to the court for the trial. The Shanghai Municipal Council was represented by lawyer Ru Baozhen, who appeared in court to prosecute. The defendant, Cao Zhengshi, hired lawyer Fan to defend her. Lawyer Ru then rose and detailed the circumstances of the cracking of the case, stating that the first defendant was being prosecuted under Article 211 of the Criminal Law for counterfeiting currency, and that the Liang Defu couple were also being charged with possession of opium under Article 13 of the Opium Prohibition Law. It was found that the main culprit in the case was Cao Zhengshi's husband, Cao Liangui, who is currently at large. However, Cao Zhengshi and Liang Defu had previously been arrested by the General Inspectorate on November 2, 1926, for counterfeiting currency and sent to the former Mixed Court for punishment. Now, they have been arrested again for the same crime, which should be noted. Moreover, the operation that has been cracked is an important counterfeit money operation, and the police urgently need to conduct a thorough investigation. Therefore, he requested a postponement for further questioning and presented the seized items to the court. Because the machines and other items were all made of iron, they were extremely heavy and cumbersome. Although they had been transported to the outside of the court by a large car, it was impossible to bring them into the courtroom. Subsequently, representatives from the banks filed a case, proving that the banknotes seized by the police were all counterfeit. When questioned, the two defendants, Zheng Caoshi and others, gave evasive answers and denied manufacturing them. After Judge Zhou reviewed the confessions, he ordered them to be remanded to custody separately and postponed the hearing for seven days.

Pan Baisan, Female Instructor at Datong University, Feared to Have Drowned Herself 95

Sudden Weariness of the World Upon Returning from Guangdong

Wrote to Friends Distributing Luggage

Pan Baisan, a former female instructor at Datong University, was from Hunan, around thirty years old, and of an upright character. She served at Datong University for a year and a half, diligently performing her duties and was trusted by the president and her colleagues. On one occasion, she had a slight verbal conflict with Director Yu of the School's Social Education Department regarding her duties and immediately submitted her resignation. However, after repeated requests from the school authorities to stay, she returned to the school in the autumn of 1931. Due to the difficulty of her work, she had no choice but to resign again and went to work in a government agency in Guangdong. Unexpectedly, last week, Ms. Pan suddenly sent a letter to her fellow townsman, Mr. Wang Nansheng, at the school, generally saying that a sense of weariness of the world had suddenly arisen in her, and when the ship arrived in Shanghai, she asked that her luggage be distributed to everyone as a memento. After searching for her whereabouts in various places, there has been no sign of her, and it is feared that she has drowned herself. The details of her weariness of the world have not yet been fully revealed.

The Sheng Family Nephews’ Inheritance Dispute Case 96

Debate Concluded, Awaiting Verdict

Zhuang Tai-furen, wife of Sheng Xuanhuai, former Palace Guardian of the Qing Dynasty, passed away in 1927. Recently, grandsons Lin Fengwen and Lin Fengjun hired lawyers to criminally accuse their maternal uncles Sheng Zecheng, Banchen, Pinchen, Yu Chang, Yu You, and their maternal aunts Guan Yi, Fang Yi, Jing Yi, and six other people of embezzling tens of thousands of dollars of their late mother Xiao Yi's due share of the property. The case was previously investigated by Judge Shen Shumu at the First Special District Court, who ordered the plaintiffs to submit evidence for further review. The day before yesterday, the hearing continued. The plaintiff Lin Fengwen was present in court, and all the defendants were present except for Sheng Banchen, who was unable to attend due to being out of town. According to the plaintiff's lawyer, his maternal aunt had written a letter to Lin Fengwen, detailing her willingness to provide him with 14,000 yuan for his wedding expenses and asking Lin not to litigate, thereby indicating that his mother, Ms. Lin, was entitled to a share of Zhuang Tai-furen's estate as inheritance. He presented the letter as conclusive proof. When questioned, the defendants claimed that they were only allocated at most 70,000 yuan and at least 10,000 yuan each, according to their mother's will. The amount accused by the plaintiff was vastly different. The defendants' lawyer submitted a petition counter-suing the plaintiff for false accusation and fabrication of embezzlement. Moreover, the plaintiff's mother passed away during the more than twenty years of the Guangxu reign in the late Qing Dynasty. The provision for daughters to inherit their parents' property only began in 1927. Therefore, the plaintiff's request is invalid. Lin's lawyer argued that the plaintiff now has two brothers, who are the biological sons of Lin Shengshi, and their right to inherit property cannot be invalidated. The amount of inheritance received by the defendants, as claimed by them, totaled only over 100,000 yuan, which is inconsistent with the fact that the first defendant, Sheng Zecheng, admitted to having over 800,000 yuan, which clearly indicates that they themselves have committed embezzlement. He asked the court to be discerning. Judge Shen declared that the debate in the case was concluded and that a verdict would be announced at a scheduled time.
